Determine validation period length (e.g., 7 days)\n        val_days = ValidationConfig.VALID_DAYS\n        val_rows = int(val_days * 24 * 60 / 15)  # number of 15-min candles\n\n        total_rows = len(df_sorted)\n        if total_rows < val_rows + 1000:\n            print(\"Insufficient data for walk-forward split.\", flush=True)\n            return {\"accuracy\": 0.0, \"bets_per_month\": 0.0, \"n_folds\": 0}\n\n        # Split: validation = most recent val_rows, training = older data\n        valid_df = df_sorted.iloc[-val_rows:].copy()\n        train_df = df_sorted.iloc[:-val_rows].copy()\n\n        # Limit training samples to most recent MAX_TRAIN_SAMPLES (controls memory/time)\n        if len(train_df) > ModelConfig.MAX_TRAIN_SAMPLES:\n            train_df = train_df.tail(ModelConfig.MAX_TRAIN_SAMPLES).copy()\n            print(f\"Limited training to {len(train_df)} most recent samples\", flush=True)\n\n        print(f\"Train: {len(train_df)} samples, Validation: {len(valid_df)} samples\", flush=True)\n\n        X_train = train_df[self.feature_names]\n        y_train = train_df[\"target\"]\n        X_valid = valid_df[self.feature_names]\n        y_valid = valid_df[\"target\"]\n\n        # Evolve a fresh population on the training set\n        pop = Population(\n            population_size=ModelConfig.POPULATION_SIZE,\n            model_types=ModelConfig.MODEL_TYPES,\n            mutation_rate=ModelConfig.MUTATION_RATE,\n            crossover_rate=ModelConfig.CROSSOVER_RATE,\n            elitism_count=ModelConfig.ELITISM_COUNT\n        )\n        pop.initialize(input_dim=X_train.shape[1], feature_names=self.feature_names)\n\n        for gen in range(ModelConfig.GENERATIONS_PER_ITERATION):\n            print(f\"  Generation {gen+1}/{ModelConfig.GENERATIONS_PER_ITERATION}\", flush=True)\n            # Evaluate individuals on training data\n            for ind in pop.individuals:\n                try:\n                    ind.model.fit(X_train, y_train)\n                    # Use training accuracy as fitness for selection\n                    pred = ind.model.predict(X_train, threshold=0.5)\n                    ind.fitness = (pred == y_train).mean()\n                except Exception as e:\n                    print(f\"    Training error: {e}\", flush=True)\n                    ind.fitness = -1000.0\n\n            # Final generation: no evolution, just report best\n                best = pop.get_best(1)[0]\n                print(f\"    Final best fitness: {best.fitness:.4f} ({best.model_type})\", flush=True)\n\n        # Skip individuals that failed training\n            if ind.fitness is None or ind.fitness <= -1000:\n                print(f\"  Skipping individual {i+1}/{len(pop.individuals)} (failed training)\", flush=True)\n                continue\n            try:\n                print(f\"  Rescoring individual {i+1}/{len(pop.individuals)} ({ind.model_type})\", flush=True)\n                # Create signals series aligned to close_prices (fill missing with -1)\n                signals_ind = pred_valid.reindex(close_prices.index).fillna(-1).astype(int)\n                # Run simulation\n                self.trader.run(signals_ind, close_prices)\n                v_metrics = self.trader.metrics\n                # Use Sharpe as fitness (higher is better)\n                ind.fitness = v_metrics.get('sharpe', -1000)\n                print(f\"    -> Sharpe: {ind.fitness:.4f}\", flush=True)\n                # Preserve validation metrics for later analysis if needed\n                ind.validation_metrics = v_metrics\n            except Exception as e:\n                print(f\"  Validation rescoring error: {e}\", flush=True)\n                ind.fitness = -1000.0\n\n        # Get top diverse models based on validation Sharpe\n        top_models = pop.get_diverse_best(n=5)\n\n        # Generate consensus signals on validation set\n        consensus = ConsensusGate(\n            min_models_agree=ConsensusConfig.MIN_MODELS_AGREE,\n            min_confidence=ConsensusConfig.MIN_CONFIDENCE\n        )\n        signals = consensus.decide(top_models, X_valid)\n\n        # Align close prices (indices correspond)\n        close_prices = valid_df[\"close\"]\n\n        # Run simulator on signals\n        self.trader.run(signals, close_prices)\n        metrics = self.trader.metrics.copy()\n\n        # For online operation, limit to most recent N days to bound runtime\n        if ModelConfig.ONLINE_DATA_DAYS is not None:\n            cutoff = df[\"open_time\"].max() - timedelta(days=ModelConfig.ONLINE_DATA_DAYS)\n            df = df[df[\"open_time\"] >= cutoff].copy()\n            print(f\"Online mode: limited data to last {ModelConfig.ONLINE_DATA_DAYS} days ({len(df)} rows)\", flush=True)\n\n        # 3. Prepare features\n        print(\"[main] Starting feature preparation...\", flush=True)\n        df = self.prepare_features(df)\n        print(f\"[main] Feature preparation complete: {len(df)} rows, {len(self.feature_names)} features\", flush=True)\n\n        # 3. ema_slow\n    df[\"macd_signal\"] = df[\"macd\"].ewm(span=signal, adjust=False).mean()\n    df[\"macd_hist\"] = df[\"macd\"] - df[\"macd_signal\"]\n    return df\n\n\ndef add_bollinger_bands(\n    df: pd.DataFrame,\n    period: int = 20,\n    std: float = 2,\n    column: str = \"close\"\n) -> pd.DataFrame:\n    \"\"\"Add Bollinger Bands.\"\"\"\n    rolling_mean = df[column].rolling(window=period).mean()\n    rolling_std = df[column].rolling(window=period).std()\n    df[\"bb_middle\"] = rolling_mean\n    df[\"bb_upper\"] = rolling_mean + (rolling_std * std)\n    df[\"bb_lower\"] = rolling_mean - (rolling_std * std)\n    df[\"bb_width\"] = (df[\"bb_upper\"] - df[\"bb_lower\"]) / rolling_mean\n    df[\"bb_position\"] = (df[column] - df[\"bb_lower\"]) / (df[\"bb_upper\"] - df[\"bb_lower\"] + 1e-10)\n    return df\n\n\ndef add_atr(\n    df: pd.DataFrame,\n    period: int = 14,\n    high_col: str = \"high\",\n    low_col: str = \"low\",\n    close_col: str = \"close\"\n) -> pd.DataFrame:\n    \"\"\"Add Average True Range.\"\"\"\n    high_low = df[high_col] - At least MIN_MODELS_AGREE models must agree on direction\n    - Average confidence must exceed MIN_CONFIDENCE\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        min_models_agree: int = ConsensusConfig.MIN_MODELS_AGREE,\n        min_confidence: float = ConsensusConfig.MIN_CONFIDENCE\n    ):\n        self.min_models_agree = min_models_agree\n        self.min_confidence = min_confidence\n\n    def decide(\n        self,\n        models: List[Individual],\n        X: pd.DataFrame\n    ) -> pd.Series:\n        \"\"\"\n        Generate final trading signals (UP=1, DOWN=0, NO_TRADE=-1).\n\n        Args:\n            models: list of trained model individuals\n            X: feature DataFrame to predict on\n\n        Returns:\n            Series of signals (1, 0, or -1) aligned to X.index\n        \"\"\"\n        signals = pd.Series(index=X.index, data=0)\n        probas_matrix = []\n\n        for ind in models:\n            try:\n                proba = ind.model.predict_proba(X)\n                probas_matrix.append(proba)\n            except Exception as e:\n                continue\n\n        if not probas_matrix:\n            # No model worked, all NO_TRADE\n            signals[:] = -1\n            return signals\n\n        probas_array = np.array(probas_matrix)  # shape: (n_models, n_samples)\n\n        # Average confidence for each sample\n        avg_proba = probas_array.mean(axis=0)\n\n        # Count models predicting UP\n        up_votes = (probas_array >= 0.5).sum(axis=0)\n\n        down_votes = len(probas_matrix) - up_votes\n\n        # Apply gating rules\n        for i, (avg_p, up, down) in enumerate(zip(avg_proba, up_votes, down_votes)):\n            # Check agreement\n            if up >= self.min_models_agree:\n                direction = 1\n                confidence = avg_p\n            elif down >= self.min_models_agree:\n                direction = 0\n                confidence = 1 - avg_p  # confidence in DOWN is 1 - avg_proba\n            else:\n                signals.iloc[i] = -1\n                continue\n\n            # Check confidence threshold\n            if confidence >= self.min_confidence:\n                signals.iloc[i] = direction\n            else:\n                signals.iloc[i] = -1\n\n        return signals\n\n    def adjust_thresholds(\n        self,\n        recent_performance: Dict[str, float],\n        target_accuracy: float = 0.65,\n        target_bets: float = 90.0\n    ):\n        \"\"\"\n        Dynamically adjust consensus thresholds based on recent performance.\n\n        If accuracy is high but bet count too low: lower min_models_agree or min_confidence\n        If accuracy is low: raise thresholds\n        \"\"\"\n        accuracy = recent_performance.get(\"accuracy\", 0.5)\n        bets_per_month = recent_performance.get(\"bets_per_month\", 0.0)\n\n        if accuracy >= target_accuracy and bets_per_month < target_bets:\n            # Too strict, loosen\n            self.min_models_agree = max(1, self.min_models_agree - 1)\n            self.min_confidence = max(0.5, self.min_confidence - 0.02)\n        elif accuracy < target_accuracy:\n            # Too loose, tighten\n            self.min_models_agree = min(5, self.min_models_agree + 1)\n            self.min_confidence = min(0.8, self.min_confidence + 0.02)\n\n        # Clamp to reasonable ranges\n        self.min_models_agree = max(1, min(5, self.min_models_agree))\n        self.min_confidence = max(0.5, min(0.9, self.min_confidence))\n\n    def get_params(self) -> dict:\n        return {\n            \"min_models_agree\": self.min_models_agree,\n            \"min_confidence\": self.min_confidence\n        }\n","numLines":123,"startLine":1,"totalLines":123}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"id":"gen-1773822339-ltinZHhR2hupD7qTlxHv","type":"message","role":"assistant","container":null,"content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"I see. The consensus logic:\n- It gets probas from each model (probability of UP class? Let's assume predict_proba returns [p(down), p(up)] maybe). The code checks `probas_array >= 0.5` to count up_votes. So if a model's probability for UP is >=0.5, it's counted as UP vote.\n- It sets direction = 1 if up >= min_models_agree, else 0 if down >= min_models_agree.\n- Confidence: if direction=1, confidence = avg_p (average probability of UP). If direction=0, confidence = 1 - avg_p (average probability of DOWN).\n- Then it requires confidence >= min_confidence (0.72).\n\nSo for a signal to pass, we need at least 2 models agreeing on direction (both voting UP or both voting DOWN) and the average confidence >=0.72.\n\nGiven that both models are identical (both random forest with same hyperparams, trained on same data), they will always agree (or nearly always). So the bottleneck is confidence.\n\nIf both models are uncertain, avg_p might be around 0.5-0.6, below 0.72, so all filtered out. The training accuracy was 0.677, so on training data they got 67.7% correct, but that's with threshold 0.5. For predictions to have 72% confidence (i.e., predicted probability >0.72 or <0.28), the model must be quite sure. That might be too strict.\n\nIn Step 14, they had MIN_CONFIDENCE=0.65 and got many bets (126/month) but accuracy dropped to 55%. So lowering confidence increases frequency but reduces accuracy because weaker predictions are included. At 0.72, we got zero bets. That's even stricter than 0.65. So we need to lower confidence to increase frequency. But also need accuracy >=65%. We observed at 0.65, accuracy was 55%. So maybe we need to improve model quality (higher accuracy) so that even at higher confidence we get enough bets. But our training accuracy is 67.7%, which is good. The problem is that validation performance is terrible (Sharpe -240). That suggests the models are overfitting or the validation set is tough. If no signals, accuracy is 0.0.\n\nThe validation Sharpe -240 suggests the models' predictions led to huge losses. That's suspicious: maybe the models learned to predict the opposite? Or the simulation is wrong? Or the models are essentially random.\n\nGiven training accuracy 67.7%, they seem to have learned something on training data. But validation accuracy is 0.0, which means that either:\n- The validation set has different distribution (concept drift)\n- The models overfit badly (depth=5 with 30 trees shouldn't overfit that badly)\n- There's a bug in validation (maybe the features or target misalignment)\n\nLet's check the walk-forward code: In run_walk_forward, after evolving the population on training, they re-score individuals on validation by predicting and simulating. Then they take top 5 diverse models and run consensus. They compute accuracy only on signals that are not -1. If all signals are -1, mask is empty, accuracy set to 0. So indeed no trades.\n\nWhy did the consensus gate reject all? Let's examine the validation rescoring: They compute pred_valid = ind.model.predict(X_valid, threshold=0.5). That gives binary predictions (0/1). Then they create signals_ind and run trader.run(signals_ind, close_prices). That simulation uses the raw binary predictions (no consensus). Then they compute metrics for each individual. The final metrics they report are from consensus over top_models. So if consensus returned all -1, it's because either agreement or confidence condition failed. Since the two models are identical, they should agree on direction. So it's confidence: avg_proba < 0.72 for all samples.\n\nWe need to check what distribution of avg_proba looks like. Could it be that the predict_proba returns probabilities that are near 0.5 because the model is uncertain? Or maybe the models are poorly calibrated?\n\nWe should inspect the model's predict_proba implementation. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"call_ad3527eb68b644d4a0c6be17","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→\"\"\"\n     2→Paper trading simulator.\n     3→\"\"\"\n     4→\n     5→import pandas as pd\n     6→import numpy as np\n     7→from typing import Optional, Dict\n     8→from .metrics import calculate_metrics\n     9→\n    10→\n    11→class SimulatedTrader:\n    12→    \"\"\"\n    13→    Simulates paper trading given a sequence of signals and price data.\n    14→    \"\"\"\n    15→\n    16→    def __init__(\n    17→        self,\n    18→        initial_capital: float = 10000.0,\n    19→        fee_rate: float = 0.001,\n    20→        slippage: float = 0.0005,\n    21→        bet_size: float = 1.0\n    22→    ):\n    23→        self.initial_capital = initial_capital\n    24→        self.fee_rate = fee_rate\n    25→        self.slippage = slippage\n    26→        self.bet_size = bet_size\n    27→\n    28→        self.equity_curve = None\n    29→        self.trades = []\n    30→        self.metrics = {}\n    31→\n    32→    def run(\n    33→        self,\n    34→        signals: pd.Series,\n    35→        prices: pd.Series,\n    36→        entry_price_col: str = \"close\"\n    37→    ) -> Dict[str, float]:\n    38→        \"\"\"\n    39→        Run simulation with fixed 1-period holding.\n    40→\n    41→        Args:\n    42→            signals: Series of signals (1=long, 0=short, -1=no trade)\n    43→            prices: Series of prices (typically close)\n    44→            entry_price_col: ignored\n    45→\n    46→        Returns:\n    47→            dict of performance metrics\n    48→        \"\"\"\n    49→        self.trades = []\n    50→\n    51→        capital = self.initial_capital\n    52→        # Combined transaction cost: fee + slippage\n    53→        entry_cost = self.fee_rate + self.slippage\n    54→        exit_cost = self.fee_rate + self.slippage\n    55→\n    56→        # Align signals and prices\n    57→        signals = signals.reindex(prices.index).fillna(-1)\n    58→\n    59→        # Build equity curve indexed by signals.index\n    60→        equity = pd.Series(index=signals.index, dtype=float)\n    61→        equity.iloc[0] = capital\n    62→\n    63→        # Iterate through each timestamp, use signal to open a trade that closes at next timestamp\n    64→        for i in range(len(signals) - 1):\n    65→            sig = signals.iloc[i]\n    66→            current_price = prices.iloc[i]\n    67→            next_price = prices.iloc[i+1]\n    68→\n    69→            if sig == -1:\n    70→                # No trade, carry forward capital\n    71→                equity.iloc[i+1] = capital\n    72→                continue\n    73→\n    74→            if sig == 1:  # long\n    75→                entry = current_price * (1 + entry_cost)\n    76→                exit = next_price * (1 - exit_cost)\n    77→                ret = (exit / entry) - 1\n    78→            else:  # sig == 0, short\n    79→                entry = current_price * (1 - entry_cost)\n    80→                exit = next_price * (1 + exit_cost)\n    81→                ret = (entry / exit) - 1\n    82→\n    83→            # Apply bet size\n    84→            capital *= (1 + ret * self.bet_size)\n    85→\n    86→            self.trades.append({\n    87→                \"entry_time\": signals.index[i],\n    88→                \"exit_time\": signals.index[i+1],\n    89→                \"entry_price\": entry,\n    90→                \"exit_price\": exit,\n    91→                \"return\": ret,\n    92→                \"pnl\": capital - self.initial_capital\n    93→            })\n    94→\n    95→            equity.iloc[i+1] = capital\n    96→\n    97→        # Combined transaction cost: fee + slippage\n        entry_cost = self.fee_rate + self.slippage\n        exit_cost = self.fee_rate + self.slippage\n\n        # Align signals and prices\n        signals = signals.reindex(prices.index).fillna(-1)\n\n        # Build equity curve indexed by signals.index\n        equity = pd.Series(index=signals.index, dtype=float)\n        equity.iloc[0] = capital\n\n        # Iterate through each timestamp, use signal to open a trade that closes at next timestamp\n        for i in range(len(signals) - 1):\n            sig = signals.iloc[i]\n            current_price = prices.iloc[i]\n            next_price = prices.iloc[i+1]\n\n            if sig == -1:\n                # No trade, carry forward capital\n                equity.iloc[i+1] = capital\n                continue\n\n            if sig == 1:  # long\n                entry = current_price * (1 + entry_cost)\n                exit = next_price * (1 - exit_cost)\n                ret = (exit / entry) - 1\n            else:  # sig == 0, short\n                entry = current_price * (1 - entry_cost)\n                exit = next_price * (1 + exit_cost)\n                ret = (entry / exit) - 1\n\n            # Apply bet size\n            capital *= (1 + ret * self.bet_size)\n\n            self.trades.append({\n                \"entry_time\": signals.index[i],\n                \"exit_time\": signals.index[i+1],\n                \"entry_price\": entry,\n                \"exit_price\": exit,\n                \"return\": ret,\n                \"pnl\": capital - self.initial_capital\n            })\n\n            equity.iloc[i+1] = capital\n\n        # Fill any remaining NaNs in equity with last value\n        equity = equity.ffill()\n\n        self.equity_curve = equity\n\n        # Calculate metrics\n        self.metrics = self._compute_metrics()\n\n        return self.metrics\n\n    def _compute_metrics(self) -> Dict[str, float]:\n        \"\"\"Compute metrics from simulation.\"\"\"\n        if not self.trades:\n            return {\n                \"accuracy\": 0.0,\n                \"bets_per_month\": 0.0,\n                \"sharpe\": 0.0,\n                \"max_drawdown\": 0.0,\n                \"total_return\": 0.0,\n                \"n_trades\": 0,\n                \"profit_factor\": 0.0,\n                \"final_equity\": self.initial_capital\n            }\n\n        returns = [t[\"return\"] for t in self.trades]\n        winning = sum(1 for r in returns if r > 0)\n        accuracy = winning / len(returns)\n\n        # Bets per month (entries)\n        n_entries = len(self.trades)\n        if self.equity_curve is not None and len(self.equity_curve) > 0:\n            period_days = len(self.equity_curve) / (24 * 4)  # 15-min candles to days\n        else:\n            period_days = 0\n        months = period_days / 30.44\n        bets_per_month = n_entries / months if months > 0 else 0\n\n        # Sharpe\n        if self.equity_curve is not None:\n            eq_returns = self.equity_curve.pct_change().dropna()\n            if eq_returns.std() > 0:\n                sharpe = (eq_returns.mean() / eq_returns.std()) * np.sqrt(365 * 24 * 4)\n            else:\n                sharpe = 0.0\n\n            # Max drawdown\n            running_max = self.equity_curve.expanding().max()\n            drawdown = (self.equity_curve - running_max) / running_max\n            max_drawdown = abs(drawdown.min())\n        else:\n            sharpe = 0.0\n            max_drawdown = 0.0\n\n        total_return = (self.equity_curve.iloc[-1] - self.initial_capital) / self.initial_capital","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":174}}}
